The Taxpayers' Association Sent a Letter Requesting the Municipal Council to Curb the Increase in Water Prices

The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating, "Dear Sirs, approved the joint letter from the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation, the Shanghai Farmers' Association, the Shanghai General Labor Union, the Shanghai Women's Association, the Shanghai Real Estate Industry Association, the Shanghai Tenants' Association, the Chinese National Products Manufacturers' Federation, and the Shanghai Citizens' National Products Consumption Association, stating that since the British-owned Shanghai Waterworks Company changed the water fee from a 25% discount to a 20% discount on February 1 of this year, which is an increase in debt, all users have strongly opposed it due to the increase in burden. On January 30, a joint meeting of representatives of various groups was held, and it was generally believed that tap water is a drink for all residents, and this public utility should aim at public welfare. In recent years, Shanghai has been affected by the January 28 Incident, and industry and commerce have been depressed, and vacant houses are lined up. Residents have launched a rent reduction movement to maintain the status quo. However, the Shanghai Waterworks Company, disregarding the difficulties of the times, suddenly took advantage of the low exchange rate at this time to deceive the Municipal Council into changing the discount and implementing the increase in tariffs. It has been decided to strongly negotiate with the municipal government and request the Taxpayers' Association to argue on the basis of reason in the case. Correspondingly, the letter stated that your association should quickly strive for the Municipal Council to achieve the purpose of canceling the price increase to maintain the market. In this time of general decline in social economy, and at a time when the world is seeking stability, fair agencies should have extraordinary rulings on actions that sacrifice the public and seek self-interest, in order to comply with public opinion and avoid accumulating resentment. The letter is approved for the above reasons, and a corresponding letter is hereby sent, hoping that you will take note and comply with public opinion."

Martyr Qian Digeng to be Publicly Buried in Wujiang

Martyr Qian Digeng was involved in the revolution and had significant meritorious service. He died righteously in Shanghai in the 16th year of the Republic of China. After proposals by Li Liejun, Ju Zheng, Wu Tiecheng, Zhang Qun, and others, and approved by the 35th Central Standing Committee meeting, he was permitted to be publicly buried to comfort his heroic spirit. Martyr Qian was from Wujiang, Jiangsu. His coffin is temporarily placed in Wujiang. According to Jin Luwang, director of the Martyr Public Burial Preparatory Committee, who is in Shanghai from Jiangsu, he is contacting various sectors regarding the public burial. The location will be in Wujiang. Once negotiations are complete, all matters can proceed. Now, a brief biography of the martyr is recorded as follows: Martyr Qian Digeng, named Gang, was from Wujiang County, Jiangsu Province. He was forthright, magnanimous, and had lofty ambitions. He studied at the Jiangxi Standing Army Training Camp and later transferred to the Army Military Police School until graduation. In the winter of the 15th year of the Republic of China, our army confronted the rebel Sun in Jiangxi. The martyr plotted an uprising in Shanghai. Before it could be completed, he was captured by the rebel general Li Baozhang on January 16th and faced death unyieldingly. The martyr had revolutionary aspirations from a young age. In the 31st year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, when Hu Ganchen and Liao Bolang returned from Japan, he was introduced to the Tongmenghui (Revolutionary Alliance). In October of the Xinhai year, when the banner of righteousness was raised, the martyr responded to the uprising in Jiangxi and went with Li Liejun to Hubei to form the Northern Expeditionary Army. After the Yangtze River was pacified, he reunited with comrades and welcomed Li back to Jiangxi to manage military and civilian affairs. During the Second Revolution, he was in charge of the military law office of the Jiangxi Governor's Office, exerting great effort. After the failure of the campaign against Yuan Shikai, he fled to Japan. In the sixth year of the Republic, he was ordered to welcome members of the extraordinary National Assembly to Guangzhou. In the eleventh year, he served as aide-de-camp of the Grand Marshal's Office and commander of the Zengcheng Garrison. He then returned to his hometown due to illness. In the thirteenth year, he served as a councilor of the Second National Army. In July of the fourteenth year, he went to the Eastern Expeditionary Army Headquarters as the director of intelligence and was transferred to be an adjutant at the Huangpu Military Academy. With the rise of the Northern Expeditionary Army, he went to Shanghai and died righteously. He was forty years old. The day after his death, his wife, Ms. Liu, prepared a coffin and mourned his death. His head was severed, but his face remained lifelike, which was praised by all who heard of it. His elder brother, Shu Fen, and younger brother, He, are both ambitious. His son, Kangmin, is already of age and will surely carry on his father's legacy.

Currently, in addition to the 100,000 yuan in cash that has already been remitted by the Central Bank, the items to be purchased are daily necessities such as towels, blankets, and bedsheets. The three committee members will be responsible for carefully reviewing and determining the final items. After approval by the committee, purchases will be made in batches and transported to America. Ding's speech briefly stated: "It is a great pleasure to gather here today. On behalf of all member companies, I welcome the four representatives of the Ministry of Industry to Shanghai to investigate the state of our insurance industry. I also hope that Chinese and foreign colleagues will comply with these rules to promote the development of the insurance industry in China together." After Ding's speech, he introduced the foreign guests to the representatives of the Ministry of Industry. Then, the chairman of the Foreign Insurance Association, Barry, delivered a speech, which briefly stated: "In recent years, your country's commerce has progressed, and various constructions have developed rapidly. Our insurance industry has also been able to develop as a result. We welcome the four representatives of the Ministry of Industry to Shanghai to exchange opinions on the insurance industry and hope that your country will implement the Insurance Industry Law as soon as possible within the possible range." Subsequently, the representatives gave speeches separately, followed by responses from Chen Wenhu, Xu Shilian, and others.

Smuggling and Drug Trafficking in North China Remain Rampant

According to a translated report from the Mainland News Agency, Dr. Wu Liande, director of the Customs Epidemic Prevention Department, recently conducted a ten-day inspection in the areas of Tianjin, Tanggu, and Qinhuangdao. After returning to Shanghai, he told people that Korean and Japanese ruffians are still very active in the private trafficking of drugs in North China, which is deeply painful due to the mental and physical harm caused to the ignorant people. Dr. Wu, a world-renowned public health expert, reportedly received reports from relevant parties that the drug traffickers in North China have organized a large-scale smuggling organization. Along the Jinpu Railway line to the north, drug-addicted farmers, shop assistants, and people from middle and upper classes can be seen everywhere. Their bodies are deeply sunken, their shoulders are raised high, and their faces are bloodless. The severity of the drug harm can be imagined. According to reports from customs epidemic prevention sub-bureaus in various places, Korean and Japanese drug traffickers smuggle large quantities of various drugs from Shenyang to Tianjin every day. They enjoy freedom of movement due to special forces. After arriving in Tianjin, they sell the drugs to farmers and shop assistants at low prices. After being disarmed, customs inspectors are often subjected to violent acts by ruffians, making it impossible for them to perform their duties. The smuggling of drugs is now gradually spreading southward from the northern end of the Jinpu Railway line. Various drugs are priced low, and drug traffickers use sweet words and persuasive tactics to promote sales, and quite a few people fall into their trap, especially young and ignorant teenagers. The main factories for manufacturing these drugs are located in Shenyang, Dalian, and Harbin, with Qinhuangdao and Shanhaiguan serving as distribution and wholesale hubs. Passengers on the Beining Railway can purchase and consume drugs from smugglers at any time in the train, because there are many drug traffickers, and the illegal protection from certain parties makes it impossible for the customs to investigate. In addition to the railway line, drug traffickers also use highways to smuggle drugs from Shenyang to various places in North China. Drug traffickers know that customs officers are powerless, so they have become increasingly rampant. Dr. Wu also stated that the smuggling in North China has not been stopped, and the customs losses have reached 53 million yuan per year.

News After the Cessation of Operations of the Inland Navigation Steamship Company

Last year, most of the steamships were leased to local shipping merchants operating on various routes, but the results were still not good. After the reorganization of the company, it repeatedly received orders from the Ministry to end the operation of the Inland Navigation Steamship Company, and it was decided to cease operations at the end of the 25th year. At that time, because the various procedures had not been completed, the Ministry approved an extension to cease operations on January 15th of this year. Regarding the agreement with Zhang Yi, the outside world does not understand the truth and there are many misunderstandings. When the Inland Navigation Steamship Company was processing its closure, a merchant named Zhang Yi contacted the Inland Navigation Steamship Company to lease steamships and docks, but it was stopped due to an event, and it was not realized. This is what happened. As for the Ministry of Transportation's decision to close down the Inland Navigation Steamship Company, it was mainly because the company was a business with additional operations. The company had already incurred losses after it took over, and it was inconvenient to maintain it. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company should focus on expanding the Yangtze River and ocean business and provide private shipping merchants with opportunities for development on inland navigation routes. In addition, it was heard that the Inland Navigation Steamship Company did sign a draft lease agreement with Zhang Yi for the lease of steamships and docks, but it was stipulated that the draft agreement would be invalid if approval was not granted within half a month after consultation. The statement that "the contract specifies that the entire handover will be handled on January 16th of the 26th year" is not factual.

Chamber of Commerce Sends Letters to Four Major Companies Urging the Use of the New System of Weights and Measures

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent letters to Yong'an, Sincere, New World, and Great World yesterday, stating, "Dear Sirs, In the instruction No. 2266 from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau on the 4th of this month, it is stated that the Biscuit, Candy, Canned Food, and Bread Trade Association of this city reported that most of its members reported that since the association unified the use of the new counter scales last summer, there have been no inconveniences in calculating transactions with each other. There are some non-member colleagues who are reluctant to change, but once they are guided, they will follow suit. However, the four major department stores standing on Nanjing Road, such as Yong'an, Sincere, New World, and Great World, use yards for measurement and pounds for weight, relying on the special areas of the concessions, and seem to be unaware of government regulations. Members reported that calculations are inconvenient and cause losses. After repeated negotiations, they have been ineffective. According to the investigation, there is a 10% difference between pounds and catties. If you want to trade with them, you must suffer this tasteless exploitation. Because of their large sales volume, you have to reluctantly endure it. This not only violates administrative regulations but also disrupts the market. After a meeting to review the situation, it was decided to report to the responsible officials and strictly ban it to achieve uniform standards and eliminate abnormalities forever. It is requested that your bureau order the immediate change to maintain consistency and facilitate transactions. According to the investigation, the new system of weights and measures has been in effect in this city for many years, and the companies should comply with it. According to the previous report, it is ordered that you transfer the order to the companies to comply with the immediate change to the new system and do not delay. It is very important to report the handling situation. In order to unify the weights and measures, it is concerned with the national regulations, and all merchants should not be unique. Moreover, your company has a large scale, and all its actions are admired by the whole city. In response to the previous orders, we write to urge you to look into the matters set forth in the order, immediately change to the new system of weights and measures, and it is our hope that you will report the handling situation."

Robber Shot Dead in Dongxi Huade Road After Struggling with Police

Female Servant Deftly Stops Robbers, Owner Suffers No Loss Two Robbers Escape, Two Pedestrians Hit by Stray Bullets

Chen Xiaoyu, 46 years old, from Shaoxing, lives at No. 105, No. 573 Lane, Dongxi Huade Road (i.e., Baohua Lane). At about 8 o'clock yesterday morning, while Chen was still sound asleep, three men suddenly approached Chen's house and knocked on the back door, each holding a bag of peanuts and persimmons, appearing as if they were delivering gifts. At that time, Chen's female servant, Chen Fang, was washing in the kitchen. She suddenly heard a knock on the door and immediately opened it to investigate. Unexpectedly, the three men

Pulled Out Pistols

Warned her not to make a sound, and stepped into the house. Chen Fang, realizing that she had encountered robbers, was not flustered at all. Catching the robbers off guard, she immediately slapped the pistol held by the leading robber in his hand onto the ground, knocking it off and onto the stone steps. She then took the opportunity to push the robber out of the door and ran to the front door, shouting "Catch the robbers!" The robbers, seeing that things were not going well, hurriedly picked up their pistols and fled backwards. At that time, two plainclothes detectives, No. 611 and No. 731, from the Huishan Police Station, were

In a Small Teahouse

Near the Xinji Bang Road, sipping tea. Hearing the alarm, they rushed over. Thus, both sides opened fire, and bullets rained down like a storm, with sounds like continuous pearls. The robbers fled while firing, and the detectives chased closely. By the time they reached the intersection of Dongyouheng Road and Yuanfang Road, the police officer at post No. 2995 also joined the chase. One of the robbers was shot more than a dozen times and fell in front of the Lester Institute of Engineering, and threw his pistol into the wall of the school. The other two robbers escaped in the chaos. The detectives then

Checked the Fallen Robber

Beside him, but he had been dead for a long time. They found a wallet in his pocket, containing 5 yuan in legal tender, and two business cards. The detectives immediately telegraphed the police station and sent a vehicle to transport the robber's body to the mortuary for examination. In addition, it was found that during the fierce battle between the detectives and the robbers, two pedestrians were injured by stray bullets near Yuanfang Road. One was Zhao Wenhua, 24 years old, from Ningbo, who lived at No. 90 Deyu Lane, Dongyouheng Road, and worked as a small worker in an iron factory.

Bullet Hit the Lower Abdomen

The other was Yu Ajin, 36 years old, from Ningbo, who lived in Zhabei and worked as a vendor. His leg bone was hit by a bullet. Both were hired vehicles to be sent to the hospital for treatment, but Zhao Wenhua's situation was more serious and very critical. The Huishan Police Station summoned the female servant Chen Fang to the police station after the incident to commend her. They deeply praised her brave actions and will praise and reward her.

Renewed Hearing Yesterday for the Case of the Assassination of Tang Youqian

The judge painstakingly sought details, repeatedly questioning the defendants.

Former Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, Tang Youyu, a native of Xiang, was assassinated on the evening of December 25, 1935, in front of his private residence, Gan Village, on Rue Ganston in the French Concession. After the Shanghai authorities offered a reward for the capture of the culprit, the former Public Security Bureau of the Shanghai Municipal Government apprehended Liu Zhennan, a native of Hubei, at 26 Rue Robert in the Siamese Concession. The Public Security Bureau also apprehended Qiu Jiyu, a bandit, and learned that he was also a principal culprit in the murder of Tang. The French police then transferred Liu and Qiu to the Special Second Court for interrogation and investigation. After a long period, the investigation was completed. The lawyer from the Shanghai Municipal Police filed a public prosecution against them for murder under Article 271 of the Criminal Law. Former Criminal Division Chief Wang Gangxu and Judge Chen Daqi repeatedly held court hearings, but the case remained unresolved. The two defendants had confessed to firing the shots that killed Tang. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, Gong Kun, the Criminal Division Chief of the Special Second Court, presided over a renewed hearing in the First Tribunal. The lawyer from the Shanghai Municipal Police, Fei Xizhen, presented the case and the articles of indictment. The court then ordered the two defendants to be interrogated separately. First, Liu Zhennan was questioned, but he suddenly recanted his confession, denying involvement in the murder. Qiu also recanted his confession. The prosecuting officer then reported that Tang Weishu, the sister of the deceased Tang Youren, had intended to testify in court today, but was unable to obtain leave from her position as a clerk in the Special First Court. Only the female servant, Zheng Li, testified. Li testified that she only heard several gunshots and then came down from the fourth floor, only to see that her employer had fallen near the second floor. She did not see the person who fired the shots and knew nothing else. Presiding Judge Liao painstakingly sought details, repeatedly questioning the two defendants for a long time. He then decided to reschedule the hearing after further investigation. The defendants were returned to custody.

Pi Sha'er Stabs Huang Kongshi Eighteen Times

The assailant asked about his missing wife; a knife wound to the forehead is quite severe.

Unexpectedly, Pi followed her to the tiger stove and said to Kongshi, "My wife has been missing for eight months. Do you know anything about it?" Kongshi replied that she did not know his wife and had no idea where she had gone. Pi then, without asking any further questions, pulled out a sharp knife and stabbed Kongshi eighteen times: one stab to the forehead, one to the right cheek, one behind the left ear, one to the right rib, one to the back, one to the right shoulder, five to the left arm, one to the left thumb, and one to the little finger. She was covered in blood and fell to the ground in agony. A police officer arrived on the scene, but the assailant had already fled. The injured woman was taken to Bethel Hospital for treatment. According to Dr. Mei, the knife wound to the forehead was quite severe and her life was in danger. The police station, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched detective He Wenjin to investigate the cause and arrest the assailant for legal proceedings.

Municipal Zoo to Host Rabbit Exhibition

Opening on the 18th of this month, registration closes on the 10th.

The Shanghai Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road, in order to promote sideline occupations for the people and improve the breed of domestic rabbits, will hold a four-day rabbit exhibition from the 18th to the 21st of this month. Registration will close on the date above. All rabbit enthusiasts, regardless of breed or location, may register with the zoo to participate. The following are the simplified exhibition rules and methods for徵品:

Simplified Exhibition Rules

(1) The name of this event is the Shanghai Rabbit Exhibition, organized by the Shanghai Municipal Zoo.

(2) The purpose of this exhibition is to promote sideline occupations for the people and improve the breed of domestic rabbits.

(3) Each entry should consist of one pair of rabbits.

(4) Different breeds must be placed in separate cages and labeled with the breed name.

(5) In order to give visitors a deeper understanding of the uses of rabbits, the zoo may exhibit products made from rabbits at the same time.

(6) If rabbit breeds and manufactured goods are displayed at the same time, diagrams and explanations must be added.

(7) Exhibitors may not engage in commercial advertising within the exhibition venue.

(8) The zoo will not charge any fees to exhibitors.

(9) In order to reward excellent breeds, the zoo will hire several experts to serve as judges.

(10) The current judging will be temporarily divided into wool breeds, fur breeds, meat breeds, dual-purpose breeds, and ornamental breeds.

(11) The judging standards for each category will be determined separately.

(12) The Shanghai Municipal Zoo will award certificates to the best entries in each category and solicit prizes from various institutions for distribution.

(13) The exhibition will be held for four days, from February 18th to 21st, 1937.

(14) The venue for the exhibition will be the Shanghai Municipal Zoo.

(15) These rules will be implemented after being approved by the Social Affairs Bureau.

徵品 Methods

(1) Registration Procedures: Exhibitors must go to the office of the Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road, Ximen, within the specified registration period and fill out a registration form with the breed, category, quantity, age, origin, value, use, exhibition area, and name, occupation, and address of the exhibitor. A registration certificate will be issued. Then, the rabbits can be sent to the exhibition with the certificate. The certificate must be presented to reclaim the exhibits.

(2) Cages and Feed: Exhibitors must rent their own rabbit cages. Feed will be provided by the zoo during the exhibition period, but exhibitors may bring their own.

(3) Registration Date: From January 30th to February 10th.

(4) Submission Date: February 17th. Those with manufactured goods and diagram explanations must arrange them in advance.

(5) Reclamation Date: February 22nd, or after 5:00 PM on the 21st.

Rickshaw Owners and Pullers Hold Separate Meetings to Protest Reduction in Rickshaws

After the Public Works Department of the Public Concession decided to reduce the number of rickshaws through a lottery on February 20th, rickshaw owners and pullers held separate meetings to protest. Details are as follows:

Joint Meeting

After the Public Works Department decided to reduce the number of public rickshaws in the concession, it was resolved that 484 rickshaws would be reduced through a lottery on the 20th, leaving 9,500 rickshaws. The owners had repeatedly opposed this decision through their association, but to no avail. The Special District Rickshaw Association held a joint meeting of representatives from the five districts at 4:00 PM yesterday, attended by over a hundred people, including Yin Zhiling, Hou Shaoan, Yuan Songmao, Wang Kunyi, Zheng Jianquan, and Bao Zhenhuang. Yin Zhiling chaired the meeting. As a result of the discussion, they unanimously opposed the Public Works Department's move and made a false resolution to seek assistance from all parties. This false resolution will be submitted to the general meeting of rickshaw owners for discussion. At the same time, the association notified all rickshaw owners to attend the general meeting of rickshaw owners at the City Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 AM on the 9th of this month to discuss countermeasures. According to the person in charge of the association, who spoke to a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency, in the past year, the Public Works Department had ordered wage cuts and forced them to pay a license fee of 1.5 yuan in January of this year. Now, they want to reduce the number of rickshaws. These rickshaws are licensed in three areas, and the Public Works Bureau and the Public Concession Bureau are following suit. Is this not forcing the rickshaw industry into bankruptcy? Therefore, the industry believes that the Public Works Department's move is not justified. At the same time, for the sake of livelihood, they are determined to oppose it to the death.

Rickshaw Pullers' Meeting

On the rickshaw pullers' side, a general meeting of representatives from the five districts was held yesterday morning, attended by fifty people. Chen Guoliang was elected chairman. The chairman first reported that if the Public Works Department reduced the number of rickshaws, it would inevitably lead to an increase of 1,734 unemployed rickshaw pullers. Including family members, the number would be over 6,604, cutting off their livelihoods, which is contrary to the principle of rescuing rickshaw pullers. After discussion, it was resolved that: (1) they would protest according to law, requesting the Public Works Department to withdraw its order; (2) if the goal was not achieved, they would take effective measures to cope with it. Then, they discussed the Public Works Department's arbitrary punishment cases and resolved to oppose the requirement of carrying a raincoat on sunny days. In addition, due to the severe weather, business was slack, and most rickshaw pullers had nothing to protect themselves from the cold, even freezing to death, starving to death, or committing suicide. However, the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association was monopolized, collecting a huge sum of 15,000 yuan per month, totaling 480,000 yuan, with no adequate relief for the poor rickshaw pullers. It was resolved to ask the chairman to follow the previous year's method and, together with legal counsel Wu Kaisheng, find ways to solicit donations of cotton clothes and white rice to distribute to the poor rickshaw pullers to help them get through the Lunar New Year. According to Chen Guoliang, a representative of the rickshaw pullers, since the Public Works Department registered rickshaw pullers, more than 40,000 rickshaw pullers have become unemployed. Now, they want to reduce the number of rickshaws by 484, and thousands of rickshaw pullers will become unemployed because they have no rickshaws to pull. Moreover, the Public Works Department not only does not restrict electric trams, buses, private rickshaws, and taxis in the concession, but is increasing their number day by day. If the Public Works Department wants to think about the public, it should expand the number of rickshaws to maintain the livelihoods of unemployed rickshaw pullers and facilitate the travel of people in the lower classes. Otherwise, it should reduce them equally. Furthermore, according to the new regulations of the bureau, public rickshaws must carry a raincoat on sunny days, otherwise they will be arbitrarily detained and punished. In recent years, theft incidents have occurred repeatedly. Once stolen, would this not increase the burden of compensation for poor rickshaw pullers? In short, the Public Works Department's move is completely unreasonable and disregards the overall situation.

Yesterday's Conversation Between Public Works Department and Reporters

Postponement of Lottery for Rickshaw Reduction; Rickshaw Industry Can Express Opinions for Reference

Yesterday, the Public Works Department invited reporters to discuss the postponement of the lottery method for reducing rickshaws. According to reports, the board of directors of the Public Works Department had previously resolved to reduce the number of public rickshaws by 500 from March 1 of this year. The bureau had announced this in September of last year and handed it over to the bureau's Rickshaw Special Committee to consider the implementation methods of this resolution. The committee had sent a letter to the Rickshaw Industry Association, asking them to express their opinions on the most fair method they believed was available for reference. The association replied that it was unwilling to express its opinions unless the Public Works Department fully explained the reasons and intentions for reducing the number of rickshaws. The Rickshaw Special Committee of the Public Works Department believed that the board of directors of the Public Works Department could handle the matter at its own discretion and submitted three suggestions to the board of directors. The board of directors resolved at a meeting on February 3 to hold a lottery on February 13. Yesterday, the Rickshaw Industry Association sent representatives to the Public Works Department to request a postponement of the lottery, citing the imminent Lunar New Year. Therefore, the board of directors of the Public Works Department approved the postponement to February 20. During this postponement period, the Rickshaw Industry Association may still express its opinions for reference.

Kuai Shitai Sues for Inheritance

Shi Feng's mother is an English woman, suing in court as an agent.

Kuai Shitai, a native of Hefei, Anhui, residing at No. 12, Lane 314, Hardoon Road, Shanghai, is involved in a lawsuit with his family in the First Special District Court over an inheritance dispute. Kuai Shitai's grandmother, nee Li, had three sons: Xiaoxian, Shouhian, and Xiuxian, and one daughter, Shuping, who was the principal of Peicheng Girls' School. Xiuxian married a Scottish woman named Huibo in England and had a son, Shitai, in 1919. He is now seventeen years old. Xiuxian died in 1923, followed by his two elder brothers. His second elder brother, Shouhian, had no children and his widow, Xu, is now alone. His eldest brother, Xiaoxian, left four children: Shiyuan, Shifen, Shisun, and daughter. After the death of Kuai Li on September 2nd of last year, she left two parts of the estate: (1) Real estate and movable property worth about 130,000 national currency; (2) A estate worth about 50,000 yuan. Shitai's widow Huibo believed her son was one of the people entitled to inherit the inheritance above. Because her son was underage, she hired Yang Linzhi, Ye Shaoying, and other lawyers as legal representatives and brought a suit against Kuai Shuping, Kuai Xu, and Shiyuan, Shijing, Shifen, and Shisun in the First Special Court to divide the estate. The lawsuit stated that apart from Shouhian, who had no descendants, Shuping was unmarried and should be equally divided with the three-part analysis by the Xiaoxian and Xiuxian. The plaintiff is the son of Xiuxian and should inherit one part. The 50,000 yuan part, apart from Shuping who had no right to inherit, should be equally divided by the Xiaoxian, Shouhian, and Xiuxian, and the plaintiff should also inherit one part. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Gongyu opened the trial, and each defendant hired Wu Baotai and Xu Jiaji as lawyers to represent them in court. They expressed objections to the plaintiff's division of the three parts. They also said that Kuai Li had a total of four sons and one daughter, but one of them, Nianxian, died before marrying, so there were not only three sons and one daughter, so the estate should be analysed as four parts. Then, the plaintiff's mother, Huibo, testified in court. She was 39 years old. Although she had joined Chinese citizenship earlier, she still did not speak Chinese, but testified in English, which was translated by a translator. Under questioning by Judge Xu, it was argued that the retreat be postponed for review.

The Municipal Party Department sent a letter to the Municipal Government to ban the increase of copper coins

The Municipal Party Department sent a letter to the Municipal Government yesterday, saying: "Dear Sir, since the government implemented the legal tender on November 4, 1935, the market price of copper coins in this city was set at 300 copper coins per legal tender yuan. The market was stable and the people were convenient. However, due to the proximity of the Lunar New Year, a general group of merchants seized the opportunity to manipulate and deliberately raise the copper coin debt, with each yuan only exchanging for about 280 copper coins. This not only violates the law, but also affects finance and endangers the livelihood of the poor. It is proposed that your government take swift and effective measures to maintain the market. We hereby send a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Government and hope that you will review and handle it accordingly."

Hui Kang Steamer Not Yet Salvaged

Another Attempt to Tow Today

The Hui Kang steamer of the Huitong Shipping Company, which ran aground on a stone embankment on the morning of the 4th while entering the port from Ningbo, was inspected yesterday morning by surveyors from the insurance company. The results showed that the bottom of the bow hold, six feet above the waterline, was stuck on the embankment. As a result, the Northern Shipping Company's tugboat did not dare to tow it at the time, fearing that the embankment would tear the bottom of the ship. The current salvage plan is to pump water into the aft hold, hoping to raise the front part of the ship's hull, and then tow it out during high tide. If this fails, another attempt will have to wait until the large spring tide next week. Therefore, the ship salvage operation yesterday failed to dislodge the vessel, and the final decision was to load the aft hold of the Hui Kang with enough coal to raise the bow, while simultaneously filling the bottom of the bow hold with a large number of sandbags, so that the hull can withstand less friction damage from the embankment stones. It is said that all work is now complete, and salvage efforts will resume today.

Requesting Central Bank to Issue More Copper Coins

The meeting resolved to ask the association chairman, Chen Kunxian, to contact the Central Bank again to request an increase in issuance. ㊁ The Central Bank is closed on Sundays. Friendship Society Initiates Long-Distance Travel to Five Provinces

The Friendship Travel Society of this city, which has been dedicated to exploration and sightseeing for over two decades, has traveled to Hebei, Chahar, Shaanxi, Shanxi, and Sichuan in the past, and has achieved remarkable results. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai in early April this year, take the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway sleeper car to Nanchang via Hangzhou, and visit the Tengwang Pavilion, Baihuazhou, Qingyunpu, and other places. Then, go to Yangshuo, and after visiting, take a boat to Xiaole, transfer to a car to Liuzhou, and visit the famous scenery such as Liyu Peak. Then, go through Hong Kong, Kowloon, Shantou, and Xiamen, and return to Shanghai in mid-May. After passing through six provinces, the trip covers more than 10,000 miles, and the scenic spots in South China, except for Guizhou and Yunnan, can be said to be fully explored. The cost is about 300 yuan per person. The detailed rules and itinerary are being printed and will be distributed to members soon.

January Statistics on Vehicle Accidents in French Concession

28 Fewer Cases Than in the Same Month Last Year

According to statistics on various vehicle accidents in the French Concession in January of this year, there were a total of 242 cases, including 31 seriously injured people sent to hospitals, 38 slightly injured people sent to hospitals, and one person who was bandaged at the police station and then sent home. In December 1936, there were a total of 252 cases, with two deaths. However, in January of last year, there were 270 cases, with one death. Compared with January of this year, there are 28 more cases, which shows that the number of vehicle accidents in the French Concession has been decreasing year by year.

She has worked in the Ximen Women and Children's Hospital in this city, the Wuhu Hospital in Anhui Province, and the Wujin Hospital in Changzhou for many years, and has achieved remarkable results. Travel Industry Association Writes Letter to French Police Requesting Investigation of Anonymous Accusations

The Travel Industry Association of this city recently wrote a letter to the French Police requesting an investigation and cessation of anonymous accusations against hotels in the French Concession. The original letter is extracted below: "Respectfully, according to reports from major hotels in the French Concession, there have recently been frequent anonymous accusations to the French Police Department and the French Municipal Council regarding violations. The authorities do not investigate and immediately dispatch detectives to search, often catching wind and grasping shadows, and the result is nothing. Travelers have already suffered unexpected panic and are unbearable to harassment. This situation may be due to malicious extortion or jealousy among competitors. The authorities must investigate and severely punish this kind of anonymous accusation, otherwise this trend will be detrimental to business and harass travelers. At this time of business decline, how can we withstand this blow? We all bear heavy burdens. The authorities do not provide protection, but lightly believe in a piece of anonymous accusation and immediately conduct unwarranted searches, disturbing travelers. We should forward a letter to the French Police Department to raise a serious protest and investigate and severely punish this matter at any time to prevent bad customs and stabilize business." After checking the association's records, the claims are indeed true. Anonymous accusations are not permitted by law. The matter should be reported to your department. In the future, if there are any such anonymous accusations, they must be investigated and severely punished to prevent bad customs and stabilize business. Sincerely, the Shanghai Travel Industry Association, February 5th, to the French Police Department.

Young Daughter of Gao Chuiwan Passes Away

Ms. Gao Yunfen of Jinshan, the beloved daughter of literary giant Mr. Ciwan, inherited her family's learning at a young age and was well-versed in the arts and literature. She then entered Datong University for two years, where she excelled in both character and academics and was highly regarded by the school's teachers and students. Starting last semester, because her marriage was approaching, she dropped out of school and stayed at home to specialize in acupuncture. Her husband, Mr. Liu Zhiquan of Wuxing, is the tenth son of the late Qing Cabinet Academician Chengru. The wedding ceremony was scheduled to be held on February 24th at the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association. Unexpectedly, Ms. Gao suddenly suffered a severe phlegm syncope a few days ago. Despite seeking treatment from famous doctors in Shanghai, there was no way to save her. She passed away yesterday afternoon, causing everyone who heard the news to lament.

Insurer Hu Yonglai Passes Away

Mr. Hu Yonglai, a senior Ningbo businessman in the insurance industry in Shanghai, held important positions in Youbang and Ningshao Life Insurance Companies. Recently, he sought treatment for mental illness at the Chinese Red Cross Hospital, and suddenly died of cerebral hemorrhage yesterday. Mr. Hu has been engaged in the life insurance business for nearly twenty years. He has always been committed to serving the society and seeking happiness and detail for others. His treatment of people has always been known for his enthusiasm and generosity. Therefore, Mr. Hu's death is not only a loss to the Chinese insurance industry, but also mourned by everyone who knew him. It is reported that the funeral will be held at the Central Funeral Home on the 7th of this month. It is expected that many people from all walks of life will attend the funeral.

Baoshan Fellow Villagers Association Moves into Pudong Building

The Baoshan Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association has been established for more than five years and has made great progress in its affairs. The association's original venue was insufficient for office work. The association has rented Room 304 of the Pudong Building at the intersection of Aiduya Road and South Chengdu Road as its new venue. The association will move in within days. In order to prepare for the construction of a new venue, the association has appointed Chairman Zhang Gongquan, Executive Directors Jin Lishan, Zhao Zhengping, Shi Wenran, Zhu Hegao, Gu Zhenyi, Yu Yaoqiu, and others to organize a fundraising committee for the venue fund, and has also hired public welfare commissioners to assist in the work. Fundraising will begin within days, and efforts will be made to complete it as soon as possible.

French Army Solicits Bids for Packaged Food

The Mixed Infantry Battalion of the French Army stationed in Shanghai now needs to solicit bids for contractors to supply miscellaneous goods, vegetables, fresh meat, food, and other items for a total of three months, from April 1st of this year to the end of June. Bids will be opened at the military grain office of the battalion at No. 75 Fulili Road at 9:00 AM on Friday, March 4th. Bidders must notify the office by letter before the 28th of this month. The winning bidder must pay a cash deposit of 200 national currency yuan and provide proof of residence in the French Concession.

Federation of Commerce Distributes Articles of Association of National Goods Joint Venture Company by Telegram

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce telegraphed the chambers of commerce of various cities across the country yesterday, saying, "To the chambers of commerce of various cities across the country: The National Economic Construction Movement Committee recently approved the establishment of the China National Goods United Business Co., Ltd. to improve the quality of national goods and promote their transportation, sales, and operation. The articles of association of the company have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing by the Ministry of Industry and are now promulgated and implemented. According to Article 8 of the articles of association, the first phase of the company should raise 1 million yuan in shares, totaling 2,000 shares, each share worth 500 yuan. In addition to the government subscribing to one-third of the shares first, the rest will be subscribed by national goods factories and national goods companies across the country. The subscription period for business shares is set from February 10th to the 28th of the 26th year of the Republic of China. Any national goods company or national goods factory that wishes to subscribe for shares should fill out a subscription form in accordance with the company's articles of association and the company's prospectus, and promptly send the evidence of share subscription to the secretariat of the company's preparatory committee (located in the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing). A copy of the company's articles of association and prospectus is enclosed for your reference and notification to your affiliated trade associations, national goods factories, and national goods companies. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China."

Agreement Signed Yesterday by Workers of Two Ships During Temporary Navigation of Xin Ningxing

After the Taikoo Company's New Beijing was brought into the yard for repairs, the New Ningxing was rented from the Sanbei Company to replace it for shipping. At that time, the workers of both ships wanted to work on the ship. After mediation by the Seamen's Union, a solution was signed yesterday. Wang Ji, secretary of the special commissioner's office, Wang Yaleun, chief of the first section, Peng Bowei, director of the branch, Mao Yufeng, secretary, Cheng Yongming, Chen Yuanlong, Lv Shuangxi, Wang Shunru, and Shao Lubai, and Wang Oumin and Xie Yucheng of the Middle Cabin Association, signed the agreement. During the temporary replacement of the New Ningxing, each shift would receive a subsidy of 20 yuan to the workers of the New Beijing, limited to six times. From the seventh time onwards, each subsidy would be 40 yuan until the New Beijing set sail. If the New Beijing could not resume sailing, the agreement would not apply.

Securities

Large Investors Spare No Effort to Boost Prices

B, D, and E Bonds Rise Strongly

Yesterday, due to the upcoming Spring Festival holiday, the market for government bonds on the Chinese Securities Exchange was strongly boosted by large investors, and the rising trend resumed, boosting investor confidence. Retail investors who were short were forced to cover their positions, and the market price slowly rose, showing considerable strength. Starting today, the Spring Festival holiday has begun, and trading will resume as usual on the 15th. At the opening yesterday morning, the market sentiment was quite buoyant, and purchases of 32.4 bonds were very strong. Sales of 46 bonds were still significant, and market prices rose across the board by 1 to 4.5 corners. In the secondary trading session, sales of 43.5 bonds were very active, and 50 bonds continued to be heavily purchased. Retail investors also covered their short positions and swapped positions, and Unified E bonds rose by 5 fen to 2 corners. B bonds for this month, however, were down by a small corner. At the opening in the afternoon, the upward trend was even stronger, with 50 bonds still being purchased. Retail investors covering their positions became even more crowded, and market prices rose another 5 fen to 3 corners. The closing trading desk still showed strong buying interest. Purchases of 50.10 bonds were still strong, and 35.12 bonds were slightly released. E and D bonds rose again by 5 fen to 2 corners. As a result of the full day, all bonds rose uniformly by 3 to 5 corners to 7 corners. A bonds rose by only 1 to 2 corners, and long-term financial bonds fell back by 5 corners. The total transaction volume was 8.2 million yuan. The comparison of price increases and decreases is listed in the table on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan).

Grain

Rumors Spread of Continued Orders for Foreign Wheat

Standard Wheat Falls About One Dime

Yesterday, the futures wheat market opened in the morning showing signs of continued decline for all months. The prices for foreign wheat were slightly lower in the American and Canadian markets, while Australian wheat rose two pence. Therefore, the market was initially stable. However, by closing, the flour market had already fallen, and rumors spread that factories in Tianjin and Qingdao had placed orders for a ship of foreign wheat, further depressing confidence. Prices fell two to eight fen compared to the opening. In the afternoon session, because the exchange would be closed for nine days, many clients holding long positions, wary of continued orders for foreign wheat, aggressively sold off. The market gradually declined three to five fen. According to market insiders, the wheat harvest in 1936 was abundant, and inventory in producing regions was higher than in previous years. As the season for new wheat in China gradually approaches, old stocks must be continuously sold off. A major shift in market sentiment is feared because of this.

Large-Scale Liquidation of Long Positions

Futures Flour Also Becomes Unstable

Yesterday, the flour market initially appeared stable but then experienced a sharp decline for all months. Prices for foreign wheat in Chicago and Canada fell by varying amounts, while Liverpool rose by two pence. Therefore, the market sentiment was initially stable, with little difference from the previous day's close. However, due to settlement, yesterday was the last day of trading, and both internal and external transactions were awaiting completion. As a result, the situation was superficially calm but inherently fragile. Subsequently, the market gradually declined. Rumors spread that factories in Tianjin and Qingdao had placed further orders for a ship of foreign wheat, totaling seven or eight thousand tons, at a price of nine yuan and ten fen. Consequently, clients holding long positions aggressively liquidated their positions, and the market became unstable. By the afternoon session, the news of continued foreign wheat orders had spread throughout the market, and outside long positions seemed unable to resist further selling pressure, resulting in a sharper decline. Prices for both near and distant months fell by a significant six to eight fen. Given this situation, the market after settlement, may see a sluggish market, and a sharp decline should be guarded against.

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources of goods from various regions showed no arrivals from the Jiangsu-Tong region. Only a dozen boats arrived with Bo rice and early rice, totaling approximately three to four thousand five hundred shi. Sales were slow due to the approaching end of the trading period. Retailers were only replenishing stocks slightly, and bulk buyers only took a little over a thousand packages of Bo rice from the Qingdao region. Therefore, the market situation remained unchanged, showing a steady state. Prices for both thick and thin Japonica rice remained unchanged, and no specific varieties had significant sales. From today, the South Shanghai rice market will close, awaiting reopening after the New Year.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, ten boats arrived from various river ports. The distribution of goods in the market was weaker than before, as rice shops were well-stocked and settlement of accounts approached. Prices for high-quality white Japonica rice weakened by a few fen to nearly a dime, while the lower-quality rice remained stable. Early rice was scarce, and prices held firm. Bo rice was weak, and white Yuan rice showed some loosening. Prices for various Indica and other rice varieties showed a weakening trend. After the close, some merchants considered suspending transactions.

Spot Cotton Consumption Weak

Spot cotton factory demand is weak. The sources are 800 packages of Yao cotton and 169 packages of general cotton.

Pledged American Cotton Was Sold Off Yesterday

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened firm due to good news from Liverpool. Overnight, traders and some foreign merchants bought, and the market rose firmly. Prices for all months rose by two to seven points. Afterwards, cotton with mortgages was sold off in the market for the first time, causing uneasiness. This led to the liquidation of long positions, especially the May futures on Wall Street. Fortunately, traders bought on dips, and the decline was slightly curtailed. Finally, short position holders covered, and prices firmed again. Export demand is expected to improve. Currently, some cotton cannot be shipped out due to the Pacific Coast sailors' strike. At the same time, Germany and Italy may also be buyers. The close was firm, with spot prices down five points and futures prices unchanged to down five points. English cotton spot prices rose eight points, and futures prices rose four or five points. Indian cotton initially fell due to hedging and selling by short position holders, but rebounded later due to buying by speculators and favorable news from Liverpool. Calcutta rose 0.75 to 1 rupee, Oomra rose 0.75 to 1 rupee, and Broach rose 1 to 1.25 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (4th dispatch).

Piece Goods

Local Merchants Suspend Business to Inventory

Cotton Cloth Trading Nearing Completion

The cloth market is flat, and transactions are gradually becoming sparse. Except for occasional transactions by distant merchants and speculators, most local merchants have stopped stocking goods, are taking stock, and preparing for the New Year. Generally, only tomorrow remains for trading, and business will resume on February 15th. Yesterday, the market was stable. Eastern fine cloth occasionally retreated slightly (2.5 fen per piece). Fine twill from local factories also fell 5 fen. Spring cloth, both high and low grades, remained firm. Yarn, whipcord, colored cloth, and coarse cloth selling prices were unchanged.

Woolen Sales Temporarily Suspended

The woolen market can be said to have completely stopped in recent days. Merchants are only busy collecting accounts and are not paying much attention to transactions. This is a common phenomenon before the year-end closing. The samples put out by the Qiu Huo brokers have also been collected. However, in previous years at this time, merchants and non-merchants often took the opportunity to buy up mortgaged goods, old stock, or closing-down stock. However, this year, because most of the old goods have been sold, this type of transaction is nowhere to be found.

Although Pure Gold Rises

The gold market initially rose due to mixed movements in overseas silver markets and continued contraction of exchange rates. London spot gold rose one penny. It opened slightly higher in the morning, but fell after major traders sold off slightly. However, buying support was still seen at lower levels. It stabilized again at noon. Later, there was another wave of selling and a further decline, but major buyers were still willing to be active. Finally, it stabilized slightly. The day's market situation is recorded below.

The morning opening was at 1151.9 yuan, up one jiao from the previous close. Chun Yuan Yong sold bars. The HSBC listing showed both British and American gold unchanged. The balancing tax was small, at 0.75, falling to 3.4 yuan. Qingfa, Yongyu, and Xinxing, among others, bought bars, rising to a noon close of 1153.7 yuan.

Statistics

Cost of Living Rises Monthly

Performance of the Workers' Cost of Living Index for January

In January 1937, the city's workers' cost of living index was 111.24, an increase of 2.19% compared to 108.86 in December of last year, and an increase of 7.33% compared to the same month last year, the highest peak since June 1932. Among the 60 items, 35 increased compared to the previous month, and 18 decreased. The average indices for each category are as follows:

Food Category: Although flour was slightly cheaper than the previous month, rice prices continued to rise. Vegetable prices were slightly cheaper due to warmer weather, but meat prices were more expensive due to the end of the lunar year. The index for this category was 104.82, an increase of 3.46% compared to the previous month.

Clothing Category: Yarn and cotton continued to rise, and the prices of various fabrics and cotton all increased accordingly. The index increased most sharply, to 106.82, an increase of 3.83% compared to the previous month.

Rent Category: According to the Bureau's recent survey, rents in various districts of the city continued to decline. The index was 112.56, a decrease of 3.61% compared to the previous year.

Fuel Category: Coal and kerosene both increased slightly. The index was not much different from the previous month, only higher by 0.16%.

Miscellaneous Category: The prices of yellow wine and sorghum were both higher, and the exchange rate for copper coins averaged only 293 per yuan, a decrease of 4 compared to the previous month, which invisibly increased the retail prices. The index was 128.73, an increase of 3.18% compared to the previous month.

Special Item: Banks and Foreign

Draft Rules for Foreign Exchange Business (Continued)

Or, for other reasons, failure to fulfill delivery, or in the event of a customer suspending exchange, going bankrupt, or declaring bankruptcy, and liquidation, etc., all transactions due or not due may be immediately closed at market prices. If there are losses, the customer is responsible for settlement, but the bank has no obligation to close the position on behalf of the customer. (Ren) The method of delivery for customers buying and selling domestic and foreign gold and silver from the bank should be handled in accordance with the rules of the relevant exchange or local customs. Otherwise, the bank may handle it in accordance with the aforementioned Xin clause. (6) Settlement Silver (Jia) The settlement silver payable by the customer to the bank must be submitted to the bank on the first business day of the month in which it is due (the difference in buying and selling). Those who offset the position with other banks, even if the settlement silver has been paid in full, the customer is still not considered to have fulfilled their responsibility and must wait until the bank has settled the position before the responsibility can be lifted. (Yi) The settlement silver payable by the bank to the customer, if the transaction has been settled in the month in which it is due, should also be paid on the first business day. If there are outstanding positions, it may be paid after all positions have been settled.

Article 7: Foreign exchange brokers (hereinafter referred to as brokers) guaranteeing foreign exchange transactions should be handled in accordance with the following clauses. (1) Brokers guaranteeing foreign exchange transactions should be jointly and severally liable with the insured party, and may not be released until the delivery is clear and the settlement silver is paid in full. Unless otherwise agreed, they may not claim the defense of Article 745 of the Civil Code (Note 1). (2) When delivering, the bank has the right to accept or reject the customer's position slips, but the guaranteeing broker may not use the high or low price in the position slips as an excuse to evade their responsibility. (3) When the foreign exchange transactions made by the customer and the bank are due, if the number of purchases and sales is sufficient to offset each other, regardless of whether it is guaranteed by the broker, the bank may give priority to offsetting without prior agreement. If the customer cannot pay the settlement silver, the guaranteeing broker should be responsible for paying the principal and interest. If several brokers have handled the offsetting transactions at the same time, the losses should be borne by each broker in proportion to the components of the transactions they have made. For the purpose of calculating the ratio of losses to be borne by each broker, the bank may close both sides of the purchase and sale at the closing market price of the day and recover the losses from each broker according to the amount. After the settlement, if one party of the transaction has a surplus, the bank may temporarily retain the surplus until all problems are solved. (4) If the foreign exchange sold by the customer to the bank is offset against the position slips of other banks, the settlement silver payable to the bank, if the customer cannot pay, and several brokers have handled it at the same time, the bank may average the prices of the position slips submitted by the customer and offset them separately against the settlement price of each purchase originally made by the bank. The losses should be recovered by the bank from each injured broker in proportion to the components of the transactions they have made. (5) If the customer suspends exchange, goes bankrupt, declares bankruptcy liquidation, or fails to fulfill the obligation of an order for any reason, the foreign exchange transactions made with the bank, whether or not they are due, should be handled by the guaranteeing broker by providing a position slip from another bank agreed by the bank, or by another bank guaranteeing delivery, or by closing the transaction at market prices, unless the bank agrees in writing. If the broker does not handle it in accordance with the above, the bank may close it at the closing market price of the day, but the bank has no obligation to close it on behalf of the broker. The losses should be fully borne and compensated immediately by the guaranteeing broker. (Note 1) Article 745 of the Civil Code: Before the creditor forcibly executes the property of the principal debtor and it is ineffective, the guarantor may refuse to pay the creditor. (To be continued)

Perhaps Mr. Pan has pioneered this path, and I hope that similar works will be created in the future, providing us with major events classified by categories for inspection, which can save a lot of effort.
