Women's Special

Embarking on the Road to War

— Hu Dui

A Word to Women in Their Boudoirs

The crisis of 1936 that the world's prophets told us about fortunately did not erupt, but the oncoming 1937 is still not very optimistic. The author is certainly not a world prophet, but Western Europe and East Asia are filled with combustible flames: Hitler and Mussolini have never changed their resolutions, and the civil war in Spain can only be prolonged and expanded. In addition, if the Eastern country, which calls itself the England of the East, still conducts its so-called military diplomacy, then the German-Japanese agreement or the Japanese-Italian communication, these things will inevitably form mutual relations due to the mutual interests of each other. So, looking at the world as a whole, our future is not optimistic. Even stepping back and looking at the space and position occupied by our country and nation, it will also make our hair stand on end!

Since the four northeastern provinces were occupied, the Jizhong-Sui provinces incident followed, and then there were rumors of the independence of the five northern provinces. Fortunately, people whose conscience has not died are unwilling to be other people's puppets, but people always think that we can be deceived, using all their energy to destroy our security. Therefore, our current position is in a state of extreme danger, and the space occupied by the nation-state has been exploited bit by bit. Therefore, from now on, all of us, men, women, old and young, must shoulder the responsibility of saving the country and saving ourselves, especially young women. For the warmth of the boudoir, now is not the time to talk about it.

We don't need to talk about any more theories. Just open our ears and eyes to hear and see. Here are teams of women going to the front lines to participate in combat or comfort soldiers, and there are teams of women participating in drills, rescue, or shooting. The time spent applying powder and rouge has been changed to making clothes and uniforms to comfort the soldiers. Beauty is natural beauty, health is natural health, without artificial decoration and affectation. As long as you can endure hardship and undertake any construction on the battlefield, that is a healthy woman.

The bugle and war drums are urging us forward, "Da Duo, Da Duo, step on the battle line, step on the battle line." This is the era forcing us to move forward. Embarking on the road to war is not a fashionable requirement, but a mobilization that everyone in China and the world should participate in. We are not fighting for ambition and desire, we are only fighting for national liberation and national independence.

Will Women Participate in Future Wars?

— Translated from the British Evening News

In the recent Spanish Civil War, women fought alongside men with great courage. Is this a precedent for future wars? If countries go to war in the future, should women be allowed or forced to go to the front lines? This has now become a question. A university professor, an army officer, and several other figures whose views are worthy of respect solemnly predict that in the next war, women will definitely be conscripted, and even British women will not be exempt. This conscription is not like in the last European war, where women only served in auxiliary corps. Instead, they will be soldiers directly confronting the enemy. I felt a chill upon hearing this opinion, but after careful consideration and assessing all the circumstances, I dare not say that it is impossible. The first thing that can be decided is that if Britain is attacked by a strong power or a coalition of strong powers, then it must resist with the strength of all men and women in the country in order to remain undefeated. After the outbreak of war, it goes without saying that all men and women of military age will be conscripted to perform the military service deemed appropriate by the government. In the final emergency, physically strong women may be ordered to operate guns and cannons. In future wars, the two armies will be far apart. Machine guns and rifles can hit enemy defenses beyond the line of sight, and cannons can fire over several miles. The newest and most lethal weapon, the bomber, can bomb concentrated troops and naval vessels with deadly poison gas bombs from the sky. These new weapons can be used by both men and women and do not rely on strong physical strength. The lightness of the machine gun is especially suitable for women's lithe bodies. As for cannons, as long as you know arithmetic and can calculate range and direction, women can use them as skillfully as men. In addition, British female pilots have shown that they can take risks and endure hardships as well as men, so aerial warfare presents no difficulty for women. It is absurd to say that the hundreds of successful female pilots in Britain today would not be able to operate fighter planes in a future war. In view of the above points, the past arguments that women are physically inferior to men and cannot wield weapons to defend their territory are now nonsense. Whether women should participate in the war is now merely a moral question, or perhaps an emotional one. However, in my personal opinion, no civilized government, no matter how militaristic, has ever dreamed of using force in this matter. The crux of the matter is whether women are willing to participate in the war. If they are willing, will men approve? In my lifetime, the nature and status of British women have changed dramatically. They share civil rights with men, have the same voting rights, can hold various occupations, and compete with men for a living in many industries. Men, for their part, are very willing for women to be on an equal footing with them, acknowledging their fundamental rights as citizens. But there is one thing they will definitely refuse: they will resolutely oppose turning women into killers. If Britain is attacked by a strong enemy, men will be as brave as before, standing up to kill and repel the enemy. They will loudly protest against training women to use guns, cannons, and bombs. In our Britain, women are greatly respected, and it would be an unspeakable degradation to plunge them into bloody and cruel affairs.

Matters to Note During the Winter Vacation

— Dan Xing

It is currently the winter vacation, and female students have already left school and returned to their hometowns. But how should they spend this month-long vacation? Some female students think that the summer vacation is for "escaping the heat" and the winter vacation is for "escaping the cold." They should temporarily put aside all their studies and order their servants all day to stoke the stove, sit around the fire for warmth, and eat and lie down, truly enjoying the blessings of a vacation. Or they might look at plum blossoms or ice skate. At worst, they might play cards with their families. Recreation and entertainment are also a kind of spiritual and physical rest, which is unavoidable during the holidays. I do not oppose it in any way, but I believe it is a great "luxury" to spend the entire vacation completely on "playing," "eating," and "sleeping." Why not use this vacation time to do some work?

Some female students may say: We are still studying. What work can we do? Household chores are done by servants, and financial distribution is done by our parents. Indeed, a comfortable living environment can foster a petty-bourgeois identity that does not know what work is. However, can the current comfortable environment permanently sustain your enjoyment of blessings, and can you permanently hide in school without going out into society? I can answer for you with certainty: Absolutely not. Neither the current nor the future society will give people the right to enjoy comfort. Men have to rely on work to earn a living. How can women be an exception? Perhaps, even today, there are still women who hold the mistaken idea that as long as they can marry a wealthy and capable husband, they can live a life of ease. This is forgivable in uneducated and unknowledgeable women. However, it is deeply regrettable if knowledgeable women still think this way.

Those many wanderers lost in confusion are waiting for insightful and knowledgeable individuals to dispel their illusions and rescue them from dire straits. How can we allow ourselves to repeat their mistakes? Only those who earn their own living can achieve true liberation, and only those who earn their own living can establish an independent personality. Therefore, we must cultivate the ability to make a living as early as possible. What we get in school is only limited textbook education. Current facts tell us that just possessing book knowledge is still dangerous for our livelihoods. The "taking risks" of college students and the suicide of a couple who were a book editor and an obstetrician, respectively, forced by life are "ironclad proof." Recently, the government has been focusing on vocational education and establishing more vocational schools for this very reason. We should be vigilant during our studies.

I sincerely hope that female students will not only enjoy the blessings of a warm stove during the winter vacation. They may as well practice household service and community service. If one person's ability is not enough, they can gather more classmates or fellow villagers to do it together. Whether it's at a weaving machine or in the fields, work has no distinction between high and low and has no boundaries. Even just the short month-long winter vacation is an excellent opportunity to train your ability to endure hardship and lay a solid foundation for self-reliance and making a living.

How to Cook Food

— Jie Fen

—Common Sense a Smart Housewife Should Have—

The most difficult task for a housewife every day is how to prepare some good food. Here are some methods for cooking common foods, which is also common sense a smart housewife should have:

Cooking Pork:

Pork is most difficult to tenderize. You can add a little hawthorn, which will quickly tenderize it while preserving its flavor. Another method: You can add baking soda, but it is not as good as hawthorn.

Cooking Ham: The skin of ham is extremely difficult to tenderize. If you coat it with white sugar before putting it in water, it will tenderize in an instant, and the flavor will be rich and delicious.

Cooking Salted Meat: If salted meat has a foul smell, add more than ten walnuts with holes drilled in their shells to the pot while cooking. This will reduce the foul smell.

Cooking White Tripe: After boiling pig tripe, cut it into long pieces, place them in a bowl, then add a little broth and steam it on top of a rice cooker. This will double its thickness. However, do not use salt, otherwise it will become hard and shrink.

Cooking Mutton: Use a whole radish, drill small holes all over it, and put it in the broth with the mutton to cook for forty minutes. Then remove the radish, and then braise it in red sauce or white sauce. This will eliminate the fishy and gamey taste.

Cooking Old Duck: When putting the duck in the pot, add a few snails and cook them together. This will make it tender and cooked quickly.

Cooking Sea Cucumber: To make it expand quickly, you can throw in small pieces of broken porcelain, which will make it expand very quickly.

Cooking Vegetables: When cooking vegetables, above-ground stems should be cooked in boiling water; underground stems should be cooked in cold water. However, sweet potatoes are an exception.

Cooking Kelp: Kelp is tough. Even after cooking it for a long time, it is difficult to soften, which is a waste of time and firewood, which is regrettable. If you add a little vinegar while cooking, it will be easy to soften and become palatable.

Cooking Black Dates: You can cook them with pith of grass, and the skin will come off by itself.

Cooking Fresh Fish: Wait until the pot is hot, then do not add oil first. Instead, rub the pot almost entirely with a piece of ginger, then add oil and cook the fish. No matter what, the fish skin will not stick to the bottom of the pot and cause the fish meat to fall apart.

Cooking Potatoes: After putting potatoes in the pot, if their color seems to be turning black, you can add a few drops of vinegar to the water they are being cooked in. This will make them white, soft, and palatable.

Cooking Eggs: When cooking eggs, wet them with cold water first, then put them in boiling water. This will prevent them from cracking.

Cooking Bamboo Shoots: Boiling fresh bamboo shoots in boiling water will make them cooked easily, crisp, and delicious. Or add a little mint and sprinkle a few grains of salt, and they will not be astringent.

Interview Notes at the Women's Education Center

— Zhang Zhang

Educational opportunities should be equal. Regardless of whether they are men or women, as long as they are human beings with round toes and square heads, then everyone has the right to enjoy education, and everyone should be able to read and write. However, despite the theoretical statement, in reality, due to the feudal idea of valuing men over women that has prevailed in China for thousands of years, it is firmly entrenched in the minds of the general public. It is generally believed that men should be able to read and write and enjoy education, while women? Under the slogan "Lack of talent in a woman is a virtue," they are deprived of the opportunity to enjoy education. What a cruel and unreasonable thing that is!

In recent decades, the call for women to enjoy education has gradually attracted social attention. As a result, in addition to the rise of girls' schools, institutions and organizations dedicated to women's education have continued to be established. (The Shanghai Women's Education Center is one of the organizations dedicated to women's education. Here, the author reports to the readers on the center's recent situation and scope of work.)

On a cold winter morning, in order to understand the actual situation of women's education centers, I hired a streetcar and went straight to Hualong Road. Upon reaching the gate of the center, I explained my purpose to the gatekeeper, and a service staff member named Wang Qing began to guide me to the reception room.

Our conversation began at this time. According to this staff member, the Women's Education Center has been established for four or five years. The director is Mr. Zhou Baoshao. Mr. Zhou's purpose in establishing the Women's Education Center was because he saw that many housewives had not received adequate education, which led them to stick to old ways in handling household affairs and lacked good plans. This has a close relationship with social order and the future of the nation. In order to enable housewives to generally acquire some common sense of managing a home, skills in handling household affairs, and knowledge of childcare and hygiene, he decided to establish this Shanghai Women's Education Center as a starting point for implementing women's education. After its establishment, thanks to the enthusiastic support of people from all walks of life, the development of the center's affairs has been quite rapid. The center holds a weekly meeting to discuss the direction of the center's work and also runs a women's remedial school, enrolling older housewives who have dropped out of school to attend remedial classes at the center. They charge very low tuition fees, hoping that older women in the vicinity who have dropped out of school will have the opportunity to receive remedial education at the center. They organize a Housewives' Association, which holds monthly meetings to discuss family problems and invite female leaders to give speeches at the meetings. They also organize a Mothers' Association, which also holds monthly meetings to discuss childcare methods and parenting issues. In addition, they organize women's vocational training classes, teaching craft skills. For example, the weaving class, which ended last December, was able to arouse the interest of women in general. In addition to these, we also publish a Women's Monthly, which publishes issues on women's issues and extracts news from the women's world, and the subscription target is entirely women."

As for the center's funding, this staff member said, "It is entirely borne by Director Zhou. If the amount is not enough, he solicits donations from the outside world. At present, there are no problems with income and expenditure. However, in order to run more businesses related to women's education, we hope that the government will provide considerable subsidies to support the development of women's education. This is something that we hope to achieve in the shortest possible time."

The clock pointed to eleven o'clock. Unwilling to take up the staff member's valuable time, I shook hands with him and said goodbye. On the way back, I silently wished the center a long and successful future, creating a great new life for women's education in China.

Idle Talk About Child Brides

— Xia Fei

Child brides are a product of the old etiquette and the old marriage system, a kind of blind marriage based on matchmakers' words and parents' orders. However, its legacy has not yet been completely eliminated, and the tragedy of child brides continues to be played out in the old families of those remote villages. If we are willing to go to these places to investigate, I believe we will find many so-called child brides, especially those who have come from child bride backgrounds.

In fact, the life of a child bride is no different from that of a maidservant, except that the title and status are different. However, we only hear calls for the abolition of prostitution and maidservants, but not calls for the abolition of the child bride system! In fact, if we want to seek women's liberation and thoroughly reform the marriage system, we must first eliminate the widespread child bride system that kills the happiness of men and women.

Although the knowledge of the general villagers is a little more enlightened than before, and they seem to be less stubborn about their children's marriages than in the past, they still absolutely disagree with laissez-faireism, and fatalism and matchmakers' words are still flourishing unabated. Especially the child bride system, which has become more widespread than in the past. Although the parties concerned have changed the name to "tong jiao xifu" (child foot wife) in order to avoid the title of "yang xifu" (adopted wife), in fact, isn't it still one and the same? It's just a clever name change.

As for the origin of child brides, although I don't know which dynasty it started in, the reasons are generally either betrothal in the womb, or because the two families are close friends, or because they want to save money and are poor. In the past, these reasons were considered very legitimate or unavoidable.

As for a girl, whether she is in swaddling clothes or in her teens, once she becomes someone else's child bride, all her fate and life will be controlled by her future parents-in-law, and her freedom will be deprived from then on. It is not until she and her fiancé formally announce their marriage that her days can get a little better. If her fiancé is a person of bad behavior, she may be threatened and ravaged by him, so the matter of "eating cold rice" and "sitting in the corner" often happens in families with child brides. If she unfortunately dies herself, there is naturally nothing to say. If the fiancé dies, then she is mostly a widow guarding the grave. Until she has lived out the three years of filial piety and guarded the filial piety, she prepares to be determined to guard the punishment and win the beautiful name of a chaste woman (?). In addition, if she wants to walk out - to marry - then in addition to seeking the consent of the parents-in-law, she must also pay a considerable bride price to the parents-in-law. On the contrary, the parents-in-law can casually marry her off to someone else, or recruit a "yellow mud shoulder son-in-law" to the house to replace their son's duties; she, of course, still has to honor them with the etiquette of a daughter-in-law serving her parents-in-law.

There are also two types that are considered upright and very common in the countryside: ㊀ is to "chongxi" (ward off bad luck); - when the fiancé is sick in bed and is about to give up hope of medicine, the family members use the superstitious custom to have the child bride marry a patient with no hope of living, send him to the bridal chamber, and eventually hasten his death due to overwork, so that the innocent girl becomes an unjustifiably a widow, "small then ends her precious youth, and the great one sacrifices her lifelong happiness: this kind of superstitious custom that is useless should be overthrown as soon as possible. ㊁ Whenever a child bride's fiancé dies, if her fate is not bad, then she will be matched with the fiancé's younger brother, which is called "one uncle takes his sister-in-law."

According to what I have heard and seen, there are countless tragic stories about child brides, and the experiences of all child brides are mostly very bad. Therefore, I deeply feel that child brides are indeed a serious problem in the women's movement!

Fourth Letter

— (Zhuo Dai)

Ms. B:

I was just about to talk to someone about the most important issue in our country's families. Now that you are discussing with me how gardens and our lives are related, what kind of great mission do they have? That day, I can take this opportunity to talk to you about it. Women are the masters of the family, so this issue should be discussed with women even more.

Family, family, everyone shouts it, everyone says it. May I ask: We call it a family, have we ever reflected on ourselves? Do some of us feel ashamed? Although we Chinese have a home, where is the "ting" (courtyard)? How many people have a "ting" in their homes? Can we call it a family if we have a home but no "ting"? This is a very serious problem for us Chinese. A Shanghai-style house, a crab-eye patio like a chimney, can this be called a "ting"? A home with a vacant lot, where washing clothes, rinsing rice, and dumping garbage are done, can this be called a "ting"? In reality, Chinese families are just homes and nothing more; they don't have a "ting."

What is a "ting"? How can it be called a "ting"? A "ting" is the garden that I am discussing with you. It doesn't necessarily have to be a so-called garden of dozens of acres to be called a garden. As long as it matches the house, there is such a vacant lot, and we think about it from an aesthetic point of view and a practical point of view, and we don't necessarily need a lot of money to arrange it into an elegant garden. This is very necessary for our lives.

We either don't have a family at all, but if we have the name of a family, we can't make it a incomplete family. We must attach a "ting" to the outside of the house. This is not a luxurious lifestyle, it is very necessary for our bodies and minds. Men, after working hard all day outside, can't be locked up in a house like being sued in court when they go back at night. In the "ting," in the flower-lit moonlight, playing with their wives, this is the joy of family. When resting on Sundays, there is no need to take a train out to travel, you can just rest at home. When friends come, they can also pass the time in the "ting."

For women, the "ting" is even more important than for men. Men go out more often, while women are at home all day. If they don't use the "ting" to regulate their spirit and body, they will sit at home with their heads down, and there will be no change at all, which is really a painful thing. As for children, running and jumping, it is even more indispensable to have such a "ting." The two words "family" were originally connected and parallel. Recently, I don't know how they have become distorted, so we must restore them.

Building a garden, everyone thinks, is a very expensive thing, but it is not really so. If the house is small, the area of the garden is naturally also small, so the cost is limited. Moreover, the materials for the garden are nothing more than trees and stones. Of course, there are expensive ones and there are also many cheap ones, and expensive materials may not necessarily make a good garden. Whether the garden is good or not! It all depends on the art of the person who arranged it. This is like painting. Using the same few pigments, some can become famous paintings, and some can only be window decorations. Therefore, if there is really an art of gardening, then it may be that a garden built with two or three hundred yuan can defeat a garden built with one or two thousand yuan. Ms.! I hope that you will come out to restore the word "family," and not have a name without substance.

Hopes for Female Writers

— Zhen

Recently, several writers in Shanghai held a "Literary Symposium" at the Youth Association. Almost all the famous writers were present, but it is a strange thing that not a single female writer could be found at such a grand event. Because this symposium was not just to gather their fellow friends to have tea and chat, but also had a greater purpose, which was to unite the entire Chinese literary world on one front to carry out a unified national salvation cultural movement. Therefore, this symposium was far from being a common social gathering. National salvation is everyone's responsibility, and female writers are no exception. Since you can write articles and run publications, you can be considered a member of the literary world. Why should a united front in the literary world leave out a part of its comrades? So I suspect that perhaps none of the Chinese female writers are in Shanghai, or that none of the Chinese women who can write articles and run newspapers are qualified to enter the realm of literature! However, under the word "unification" in the literary world, it is inevitable to feel regrettable!

Therefore, it makes me feel even more that female literary authors have been too silent in recent years! In addition to a few seniors who were once very popular seven or eight years ago, there are not many rising stars. Although there are several women's publications in Shanghai, there are not many mass reading materials that can be taken out and are popular all over the country. There are very few works like Ms. Bing Xin's "Letters to Young Readers" that she used to write. No wonder the literary world has forgotten female writers!

I neither understand literature nor dare to express my opinions rashly. Now I am using the qualification of a young student to hope that the talented female writers, or rather the female compatriots who can write articles, will make great efforts in the literary movement and produce more literary works that save the country and save the people. If the female writers can also hold a female literary symposium to organize some kind of association to work together and research together to produce a large number of national salvation literature, then that would certainly be what I sincerely pray for.

Correspondence

Mr. Editor: I have just read your publication's issue number 48, containing a Tokyo dispatch titled "A Huge Disturbance That Shocked Students Studying in Japan," and I was extremely astonished after reading it. The article ostensibly concerns the "women's liberation issue" but is actually a vent for personal resentment. I am writing to present the essentials of the matter based on the facts:

(1) Jin Did Not Go Insane: The passage stating, "According to a friend close to Wei Jin, he feigned mental illness to shirk responsibility," is entirely fabricated. Although Jin's wife, Ms. Zeng Yi, became pregnant in 1934 and was admitted to Juntendo Hospital in Tokyo for a threatened miscarriage, he experienced digestive, nasal, and sleep disorders for two years due to the stress of comforting his wife, but he did not go insane.

(2) Jin Did Not Distribute Leaflets: Although Ms. Fei wishes to attribute baseless accusations to Jin by claiming he is insane, it is just as absurd as her accusing Jin of murdering Zeng Yi and oppressing women at the Office of the Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan, because her only evidence accusing Jin of murder is her own "dream." As for the numerous reasons that can prove Jin did not distribute leaflets, the most prominent are: (1) Jin did not go insane. (2) Jin does not engage in such absurd activities. (3) Jin has not seen the so-called leaflets to this day. (4) The Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department sent someone to advise Jin that he could sue them legally, but Jin declined with gratitude. (5) Jin has no economic relationship with Ms. Fei, so there is no question of "swindling money"; moreover, they are not close friends, and he does not know Ms. Fei's character in detail.

(3) The Relationship Between Jin and Ms. Zeng Yi: Jin and Ms. Zeng Yi not only have five or six years of marital life but also have three children together, although it was a love marriage, they obtained the consent of both sets of parents. They had a simple wedding reception and received gifts from relatives and friends. Regarding the monetary gifts from both parents, although Ms. Fei brought her to the Office of the Supervisor and filed for divorce on December 23, 1935, Jin has not agreed because her reason for falsely accusing Jin of murder based on a "dream" is untenable. In short, Jin and Ms. Zeng Yi are not only not divorced but also have a long-standing marital relationship, a happy family, and the burden of raising children. Even today, Jin cannot help but love his children's mother, Zeng Yi.

The above is written entirely based on facts, without any falsehoods. I hope that the editor will maintain an impartial attitude and publish it in the newspaper, which will not only protect existing families with children but also prevent young men and women from going astray on the wrong path of "trifling with life." Respectfully, I wish you good health and request your guidance! Wei Jin, January 25th

After Marriage

— (Huan Yue)

In order to lighten his burden a little, I finally re-entered society in the second month after our marriage!

Luckily, after only two months of probation, my salary has increased from forty yuan to sixty yuan!

Indeed, in this day and age, the gray city of Shanghai is filled with economic depression. Most small businesses have either closed down or are being liquidated. The larger companies that still exist are busy laying off employees and reducing salaries, let alone considering raises. Indeed, I feel very satisfied with this!

Just a small clerk—a typist at a customs brokerage—able to earn two yuan a day without much effort. That's not easy, is it! I often comfort myself this way!

Indeed, I believe nothing is truer than the saying "contentment brings happiness." I think that the place where he works is too far away from me. Unless there is a special event, we will never see each other during the day because we both have our lunches catered by nearby restaurants!

We are both a bit childish and like to walk together. Every evening, I stroll from Jiangxi Road into Nanjing Road, and he comes over from Jing'an Temple Road. Whether one of us is early or late, or whether it's raining or snowing, we wait at the Shanghai First Department Store tram stop!

Sometimes, after dinner, we go to a nearby second-run theater to watch a domestic film, and maybe even listen to storytelling. This is how we spend our days!

He loves to hold small children. Sometimes we bicker about this, and he tidies his clothes and slips outside. I refuse to give in and go into the side room to play cards. After he returns, we laugh and joke again!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Abolishing the Long Gown and Mandarin Jacket

— Tian Yu

Speaking of the long gown and mandarin jacket, this was the most imposing and legally recognized "formal attire" in our country for the past seven or eight years. Not long ago, General Song Zheyuan specially noted on his invitations to entertain guests: Attendees must wear "blue gown and black mandarin jacket." Furthermore, at important state ceremonies, when the president receives foreign envoys, those who shuffle and stumble are all in blue gowns and black mandarin jackets. Group weddings held in Shanghai also stipulated that the groom's formal attire should be a blue gown and black mandarin jacket. Now, Singaporean overseas merchant Chen Jiageng has telegraphed the National Government, requesting that the formal attire of the long gown and mandarin jacket be abolished. He stated that "the long gown and mandarin jacket are remnants of the Qing dynasty's clothing system, no longer appropriate for the times, and should have been abolished long ago. Continuing to adhere to them as formal attire negatively influences the national psyche and hinders national revival," and so on. Following the same telegram, there is the following annotation: "The clothing system regulations promulgated in 1929 are currently under revision, and the Ministry of Interior has drafted a proposal that is under review." It is possible that the long gown and mandarin jacket, previously designated as one of the eight formal attire options, may be abolished altogether.

The minor matter of clothing may seem unrelated to national welfare and people's livelihoods. However, ever since our ancient ancestors proclaimed, "If one's attire is not proper, disaster will befall the person," the matter of clothing has become very important and complicated. Before the Republic of China, clothing systems throughout the dynasties had distinctions in rank. It goes without saying that there was a great divide between officials and commoners. Even the blue-robed scholars, the so-called literati, had specific scholars' turbans and robes that commoners could not wear casually. One can learn about this by reading *The Scholars*. After the Republic of China, these distinctions naturally no longer existed. However, some people still implicitly acknowledge that clothing is related to some grand principles. The long gown and mandarin jacket embody the principle of preserving Eastern spiritual civilization. The clothing system initially established in the early years of the Republic of China was the Western swallowtail formal dress, clearly derived from foreign forms. The long gown and mandarin jacket are unique to China, and it is most appropriate to say that they preserve Eastern traditional virtues. However, according to Chen Jiageng's telegram, this attire is a remnant of the Manchu Qing dynasty. From a national perspective, it is also a kind of foreign attire. Only because it has been used for a long time has the foreign thing become something inherent. I remember an essay by Mr. Lu Xun about "beards." It is said that the upturned two-cornered beard that is currently popular in Japan was originally a Han Chinese beard style that was transmitted there, while the flat, downward beard that Chinese people now keep is precisely the beard style of the northern barbarian tribes. However, after a long period of transmission, some people mistakenly believe that the Japanese beard style is Japanese and that we should not learn it, while the flat beard is unique to China and is considered to be inherited from our ancestors! This is the same situation as people not realizing that the long gown and mandarin jacket were originally clothing of the Qing dynasty. If Mr. Chen had not pointed it out, we would have forgotten.

In recent years, Chinese traditional spirit has been greatly emphasized in various aspects. Architecture is one example, with painted beams and carved pillars flourishing for a time. However, the content is entirely based on foreign methods, which is also a kind of contradiction. Insisting on preserving all inherent things today, while the spirit may be admirable, often gives a sense of being strenuous and unrewarding. Rather than this, it is better to let history take its course. Discussing clothing led me to these reflections.

The Lighthouse Keeper

— Li Liwen

Since I was little, my excessively compassionate heart has been moved to trembling by many trivial things.

When I was fourteen years old, my father had to move from Bandung—the place where I grew up—to Cibugis, a quiet seaside town in Cilacap, due to business failures.

There: there were no schools. There was only a long, winding stretch of white sand beach shimmering in the sunlight, the vast blue sea constantly crashing against the shore with white waves, and two stone dikes extending far into the sea, embracing like crab claws—from the shore, one could still see a short tower at the end of each dike, each emitting light throughout the night. In addition, there was what else? A clear blue and lovely sky, perhaps. That watched over the fishermen as they went out to sea in the faint dawn, and watched over them as they rocked back in their small boats in the afterglow of dusk.

I felt lonely.

Every day, I would wander along the beach, picking up shells, digging into the sand to catch small crabs, or go to the woods to find a shady, grassy place to lie down—however, you would always sigh. How can people escape the life of grouping together?

One day, the luminous stone dike that stretched far into the embrace of the sea suddenly aroused my infinite curiosity. I tried walking along the dike—to the front of the lighthouse on the left. The Malay old man who looked after the tower was surprised and befriended me. Afterwards, every morning I would walk along the dike surrounded by the sea and spend the day with the old man; when the sea gently stirred up the wind, and the seagulls and eagles began to circle low above the waves, the old man would send me out of the tower gate.

The old man was lonely. The sea breeze had hunched him over, and the waves made him unable to hear sounds lower than the waves. However, his eyes were sharp, seeing as far as the sea, seeing as clearly as an eagle.

The old man liked to tell stories. He had spent most of his life listening closely to the sound of the waves, and had come up with many stories.

"...Ah, he is a very loving and kind old man! You will not find him in the world, because the devil has made everyone bad—but he will emerge from the sea..."

The old man liked to start like this. He often brought his head almost to my face, and that's how I listened to him speak and tell his stories.

"But won't he drown?"

"No," the old man laughed, his eyes deeply buried in wrinkles. "How can he drown? The white waves that rise and fall are the old man's breath...! When there are too many evil people, the old man will come out, catch the evil people in a big bag, and take them to the depths of the sea..."

The old man made me fantasize. The old man's stories wove a beautiful and lovely picture in my imagination. When I was lonely, I would melt into my illusions, as if I saw the kind and just old man, the fairy of the sea, and the beautiful and tranquil world.

Later, my father had to move the family to the capital, Batavia. When the old man put his ear to my mouth and heard this news, he shook his head, and gently

Breaking Free from the Clutches of Death

— Xing

In pictures, we can see Death painted, wearing black clothes, wearing a black hat, with eyes that are just two black holes, a mouthful of sharp teeth, and a pair of hands with sharp claws, causing people to die!—The reasons for people's deaths are different, but most are due to illness; so it can also be said that Death uses "illness" as the only tool for killing. However, if people receive appropriate treatment when they are sick, even if they are very ill, they can break free from the clutches of Death.

Appropriate treatment is nothing more than good doctors and good medicine. The Wuzhou Pharmacy has doctors for this purpose and specializes in producing more than three hundred kinds of effective household medicines. It also has consulting rooms for famous doctors of various departments in the building on Fourth Road. The main consultants are the most famous doctors in Shanghai. In this way, those with minor illnesses only need to take over-the-counter medicines, and those with more serious illnesses can seek medical treatment, so there is no way that misfortune cannot be turned into good fortune.

New Year's Eve Dinner

— Xin Yun

In a living room, there is a table full of food, with dishes of various kinds, and the old and young are sitting around the table, laughing and talking lively: The stove is burning with a raging fire, forgetting the cold; this is the scene of the Li family eating New Year's Eve dinner.

Mrs. Li is already nearly fifty years old, and she is in particularly good spirits today. She ate many dishes and even ate two bowls of rice. She also looked after the children and earnestly urged others to eat, and her spirit was not tired at all.

I remember that last year, Mrs. Li was suffering from anemia, her face was pale, her hands and feet were often cold, and she didn't feel any taste in her food! And she was mentally exhausted! Since she took "Zilai Blood," her complexion has gradually become rosy, her appetite has gradually increased, and all her symptoms have suddenly disappeared, so she can have the joy of eating New Year's Eve dinner today.

said, looking out at the sea from the window:

"I am a lonely person again!"

From Cibugis to Batavia, and for the six years that followed—until now, from Java to Sumatra, to Borneo, and even back to my homeland in the Pearl River or the Yangtze River basin, the threads of my journey have stretched further and further. However, whenever I see the sea, or when a big wind sweeps up at night, I often think of the lighthouse keeper of Cibugis, and his desolate days surrounded by the waves.

"Bless him! The lonely old man!"

I often pray silently.

New Year in My Hometown

— Shi

In the New Year in my hometown, the most interesting thing for children is the "lion dance."

Each lion dance troupe has about thirty to forty people at most, and more than twenty people at least. Everyone wears the same clothes and ties a belt around their waist, and they are all brave and upright. As soon as the opening cannon of New Year's Day sounds, they start to perform the lion dance at people's homes. The most prosperous period is from New Year's Day to the fifth or sixth day of the new year, and after the fifth or sixth day, it gradually becomes less common. There are four types of lion dance troupes:

Qilin: This is mostly organized by residents of the city, and there are also villages in neighboring cities. This type of lion dance is the most outstanding because it has the most people and the equipment is also neat. The gongs and drums consist of a large cymbal, a loud drum, and a thick copper gong, which sound very loud and majestic. A unicorn head is made of bamboo and paper paste, given beautiful colors, and the whiskers and hair are made of velvet. A cloth of ten feet long and four feet wide is painted with colorful patterns to make the body. At the end of the cloth, a bunch of velvet is used to make the tail. When dancing, one person holds the unicorn head with both hands, and one person bows and bends over at the end of the tail. As soon as the gongs and drums sound, the two people dance various poses in the arena. After the dance, they perform boxing and staff, followed by one-on-one comparisons of weapons such as double knives and spears.

Lion: Most come from nearby villages. The performance is similar to the former, but the gongs and drums are different. The lion's head is flat and round, with a diameter of about two feet. One drum and two gongs are smaller than the former, and the sound is not as loud as the former. The knives, spears, and shields are also relatively small, but some add performances of several people comparing staffs and jumping on tables.

Guest Lion: These are also mostly played by nearby villages. They are probably very similar to "Lion," but the lion's head is not flat and round: it is more than a foot large and looks like a cat's head, and the mandible is movable and can be opened and closed. There are also four people outside the door, wearing masks, two in the shape of monkeys, and two as simpletons, following the lion's dance and making various humorous movements.

Out-of-Town Lion: These all come from other towns. The number of people is relatively small, and the lion's head and gongs and drums are the same as the Guest Lion, but there are no masks. The skills are relatively sophisticated. They often use several tables, and people perform various tricks on the table top.

In addition to the above four types of lion dances, the two that adults welcome more are "lantern wine" and "flower lanterns."

Lantern Wine: On the Lantern Festival, every family must prepare sacrificial offerings to worship the gods and ancestors. On this day, families in the streets and alleys who have raised boys in the past year will set up banquets. If there are families with public property in the clan, then the public will handle the banquet and drink in the ancestral hall. This is called "Lantern Wine." On this night, the bright moonlight and the brilliant lights reflect, doubly loud, mixed with the shouts and laughter of children. Groups of men and women stroll on the streets, watching flower lanterns and swings. The children carry paper lanterns and run around and pour wine randomly, wanting to be crazy with joy. This will continue until late at night before stopping.

Flower Lantern: Lanterns are made of straw and colored paper into figures and pavilions, arranged in a ring next to a tower-shaped frame made of bamboo strips and colored paper, or arranged next to a wooden frame about eight or nine feet long. This is called "Flower Lantern." This kind of flower lantern is mostly hung in the center of larger temples for people to enjoy. After the Lantern Festival, each person uses a strip of red paper and signs a "Respectfully requesting a flower lantern frame" and pastes it under the flower lantern. On the seventeenth day, the temple keeper of the temple will throw the paper signs pasted by each person in front of the gods one by one. The one with the most holy signs (one yin and one yang) will be given this flower lantern frame. When sending it, they beat gongs and drums all the way, playing fine music, and setting off firecrackers, which is also very lively.

In the dreary rain and sorrowful wind of the third watch of the night, tossing and turning in bed, unable to find peace. Like the weeping of a cuckoo, suddenly evoking memories of childhood. Like intertwined branches, like two hearts beating as one, destined by fate in a previous life. Tears streamed down as we parted, and countless springs have passed in a flash. I trust you are happy with your husband, while I remain a pure and innocent virgin. Even the magpie bridge allows the Cowherd and Weaver Girl to meet, can we be together again in this life? Day and night, the thought breaks my heart.

New Contributions from the Paris Theater

The Paris Theater, known for holding the screening rights of six major companies, has always been committed to serving the community. With brand new projectors and clear sound and light, it selects films carefully, taking the best and extracting the essence. The excellent reputation it has earned over the past year is universally acknowledged. Recently, it signed a contract with United Artists, an authority in the film industry. Films such as Chaplin's "Modern Times" will also be shown at the theater in turn. Holding so many screening rights is unprecedented among all theaters in Shanghai. It is also rumored that starting from the eve of the abolished lunar new year, the world-renowned all-color feature film "Ramona" has been selected. Anticipating crowds, early screenings will be added from the first to the fourth day of the lunar new year. Shanghai Grand Theater Shows "Paradise on Earth" During the Abolished Lunar New Year

The dazzling and unparalleled great color love giant film "Paradise on Earth" will be publicly screened at the Shanghai Grand Theater during the old lunar new year. Color films have always been an experiment in Hollywood, but "Paradise on Earth" has reached the pinnacle of perfection and beauty. The director uses the extraordinary strengths of color films everywhere, using moving shots to poetically reveal the most complex, most wonderful, and most highly exciting emotions and images. The protagonist in the film is the mysterious actress Marlene Dietrich. Marlene's previous films have long been household names. In this film, she plays a lovestruck young girl, demonstrating even more consummate skill. Co-starring with her is Joel McCrea. Since Joel's debut in "These Three," this film is truly the actor's masterpiece, it is said.

The Beginning of the Theater Year: "1937 Theater Society" is Born

There is no doubt that 1937 is considered the year of theater. Following public performances by Zhonglu and amateur groups, the "1937 Theater Society" has also emerged in response and will soon announce its birth, holding its first public performance in a brand new manner.

The naming of the "1937 Theater Society" is perfectly suited to the significance of the year of theater and will undoubtedly remain a memorial in the history of Chinese theater. They are currently actively preparing, and the script is said to be temporarily unannounced, but it is expected to be a powerful work of national defense drama.

Xie Jun in "New Year's Money"

A young painter, a young man with artistic cultivation and enthusiasm, with an active and burning heart, jumped into the film garden. His dedication, his efforts, and the future glorious harvest can be guaranteed.

Xie Jun, his joining the cast of Mingxing Film Company was not long ago, but his name is already quite familiar to the audience. In "Night Meeting," he played a纨袴 young master, performing the personality and behavior of that kind of person vividly and thoroughly. His amazing talent has since given people a considerable understanding. In "Living and Dying Together," "Qingming Season," and recently "The Eternal Smile," he has played very important roles. The future of this newcomer is bright and splendid.

Now, in Zhang Shichuan's new film "New Year's Money," he plays the father of a poor child, Xiao Sanzi, wearing old and dirty clothes, a couple with Shu Xiuwen, living in a small thatched hut. His child goes everywhere to pick up garbage every day. One day, he accidentally finds a dollar in the trash can, and happily rushes home to show Xie Jun and his wife.

"One dollar" is unremarkable to some people, but for those who are struggling to make ends meet, it is like finding a treasure. The couple competes to look at it, and all the neighbors around come to admire this "one dollar." With many people and many hands, snatching and grabbing, suddenly a fire breaks out in one of the thatched huts. Everyone is busy putting out the fire, and the cries and shouts create chaos. As a result, these many thatched huts are all destroyed for looking at "one dollar," and from then on, that dollar is also buried in the burned site. In this scene, Xie Jun's performance is particularly moving. When it is publicly screened, you will know that this statement is true.

Bai Yang's Dream

Silver moon, silver stars, silver weeping willows, silver plantain, silver grass… In this all-silver garden, Bai Yang, the heroine of "Crossroads," dressed in a 19th-century French girl's costume, exposing her snow-white shoulders and arms, innocently and happily sitting on a swing.

Her beloved, Zhao Dan (the hero of "Crossroads"), came. She smiled warmly and waved to Zhao Dan. Zhao Dan approached her, and the flames of love hidden in their hearts burned passionately, embracing tightly, kissing, kissing.

However, with the sound of a rooster crowing, Bai Yang's dream woke up. She was not in the silver garden, and her beloved Zhao Dan was nowhere to be seen. She felt disappointment and sadness.
